If you want to get photos of Red-breasted Nuthatches foraging on rabbit brush or Lark Buntings feeding in the desert with Vesper Sparrows then this is the place to go.----I thought it would be interesting to compare the birds seen last week at Porter Springs with the birds seen this week. URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS653885448	2019-11-05 17:05:29	10564	species	Lewis's Woodpecker	Melanerpes lewis			31				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Storey	US-NV-029		9			McCarran Ranch	L8493880	H	39.5460212	-119.5710984	2018-09-03	10:33:00	obsr88222	S48267768	Incidental	P20	EBIRD				1	0		1	1	0		EDIT: The north side of McCarran Ranch is actually in STOREY Co. (not Washoe -- it and nearby parcels of land were transferred from Washoe to Storey around the time that TNC acquired the property) therefore this checklist was moved from the McCarran Ranch (Washoe Co.) hotspot to the main McCarran Ranch hotspot (located in Storey Co.).	A conservative count (I may have missed a few at the front of the flock) of a loose flock of at least 31 inviduals, flying high upriver (towards the west). A few eventually crossed over to the south side of the river (Storey Co.) near the ranch house on the north side, where the canyon narrows towards the west end of the McCarran Ranch. Interestingly, the birds didn't seem to follow the river beyond this point, sticking to their heading and staying north of the river instead of veering southwest with the river (perhaps they were headed west towards the Sierras to winter in California, and not headed south through Carson City area?).----These were initially seen at a distance, and my gut said Lewis's, however after counting at least 31 of them streaming by in a loose flock, I doubted my ID and figured they must have been Pinyon Jays.  Weeks later, on 28 Oct, I finally got the photos off my camera (these seemed inconclusive looking at the small LCD screen on my camera at the time) and immediately thought the structure was indeed a better fit for Lewis's than Pinyon Jay. A short while later, enough details were visible on a few birds to confirm that ID.  It's worth mentioning that the high count for Lewis's Woodpecker in NV, according to eBird, was on 2 September 2007, when Mark Lenz had a count of 56 along Middle Fork Jakes Creek Road north of Wells up towards the Idaho border (just 1 Julian day earlier than this observation).
